### Core Classes and Functions

1. **Main Application Class (`SportsApp`)**

   - **Methods**:

     - `load_model`: Loads the YOLO model using ONNX.
     - `start_video`: Starts capturing video from the camera.
     - `process_frame`: Processes each video frame for object detection and overlays.
     - `update_overlay`: Updates the video overlay with detected objects.

2. **Object Detection Class (`ObjectDetector`)**
   - **Purpose**: Handles the loading of the YOLO model and performs object detection.
   - **Methods**:
     - `__init__`: Initializes the object detector with the model path.
     - `detect_objects`: Runs the detection on a given frame.

3. **Video Processing Class (`VideoProcessor`)**
   - **Purpose**: Manages video capture and processing.
   - **Methods**:
     - `__init__`: Initializes video capture.
     - `get_frame`: Captures a frame from the video feed.

4. **GUI Class (`AppGUI`)**
   - **Purpose**: Sets up the graphical user interface using Tkinter.
   - **Methods**:

### File Structure

1. `main.py`
2. `object_detector.py`

### Implementation

#### 1. `main.py`

```python
'''
Main application file for the sports app that handles video processing and overlays.
'''

from app_gui import AppGUI
from video_processor import VideoProcessor
from object_detector import ObjectDetector
import cv2

class SportsApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.video_processor = VideoProcessor()
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
        self.gui = AppGUI(self.start_video)

    def load_model(self):
        # Load the YOLO model using ONNX
        pass

    def start_video(self):
        # Start capturing video from the camera
        while True:
            frame = self.video_processor.get_frame()
            if frame is None:
                break
            self.process_frame(frame)

    def process_frame(self, frame):
        # Process each video frame for object detection and overlays
        detections = self.object_detector.detect_objects(frame)
        self.update_overlay(frame, detections)

    def update_overlay(self, frame, detections):
        # Update the video overlay with detected objects
        for detection in detections:
            x, y, w, h = detection['bbox']
            cv2.rectangle(frame, (x, y), (x + w, y + h), (0, 255, 0), 2)
        cv2.imshow('Sports App', frame)
        cv2.waitKey(1)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = SportsApp()
```

#### 2. `object_detector.py`

```python
'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''

import cv2
import numpy as np

class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)

    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections

    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                score = detection[4]
                if score > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    bbox = detection[:4].astype(int)
                    detections.append({'bbox': bbox, 'score': score})
        return detections
```

#### 3. `video_processor.py`

```python
'''
Video processing class that captures video frames from the camera.
'''

import cv2

class VideoProcessor:
    def __init__(self):
        self.capture = cv2.VideoCapture(0)

    def get_frame(self):
        # Capture a frame from the video feed
        ret, frame = self.capture.read()
        if not ret:
            return None
        return frame

    def __del__(self):
        self.capture.release()
```

#### 4. `app_gui.py`

```python
'''
Graphical user interface class for the sports app using Tkinter.
'''

import tkinter as tk

class AppGUI:
    def __init__(self, start_video_callback):
        self.window = tk.Tk()
        self.window.title("Sports App")
        self.start_button = tk.Button(self.window, text="Start Video", command=start_video_callback)
        self.start_button.pack()
        self.window.mainloop()
```

### Summary

This implementation provides a structured approach to creating a sports app that utilizes YOLO for object detection and overlays in real-time video. The application is designed to be compatible with mobile devices by using efficient libraries and frameworks. Each component is modular, allowing for easy updates and maintenance.

'''
Main application file for the sports app that handles video processing and overlays.
'''

from app_gui import AppGUI
from video_processor import VideoProcessor
from object_detector import ObjectDetector
import cv2

class SportsApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.video_processor = VideoProcessor()
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
        self.gui = AppGUI(self.start_video)

    def load_model(self):
        # Load the YOLO model using ONNX
        pass

    def start_video(self):
        # Start capturing video from the camera
        while True:
            frame = self.video_processor.get_frame()
            if frame is None:
                break
            self.process_frame(frame)

    def process_frame(self, frame):
        # Process each video frame for object detection and overlays
        detections = self.object_detector.detect_objects(frame)
        self.update_overlay(frame, detections)

    def update_overlay(self, frame, detections):
        # Update the video overlay with detected objects
        for detection in detections:
            x, y, w, h = detection['bbox']
            cv2.rectangle(frame, (x, y), (x + w, y + h), (0, 255, 0), 2)
        cv2.imshow('Sports App', frame)
        cv2.waitKey(1)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = SportsApp()
```

#### 2. `object_detector.py`

```python
'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''

import cv2
import numpy as np

class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)

    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections

    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                score = detection[4]
                if score > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    bbox = detection[:4].astype(int)
                    detections.append({'bbox': bbox, 'score': score})
        return detections
```

#### 3. `video_processor.py`

```python
'''
Video processing class that captures video frames from the camera.
'''

import cv2

class VideoProcessor:
    def __init__(self):
        self.capture = cv2.VideoCapture(0)

    def get_frame(self):
        # Capture a frame from the video feed
        ret, frame = self.capture.read()
        if not ret:
            return None
        return frame

    def __del__(self):
        self.capture.release()
```

'''
Main application file for the sports app that handles video processing and overlays.
'''
from app_gui import AppGUI
from video_processor import VideoProcessor
from object_detector import ObjectDetector
import cv2
class SportsApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.video_processor = VideoProcessor()
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
        self.gui = AppGUI(self.start_video)
    def load_model(self):
        # Load the YOLO model using ONNX
        pass
    def start_video(self):
        # Start capturing video from the camera
        while True:
            frame = self.video_processor.get_frame()
            if frame is None:
                break
            self.process_frame(frame)
    def process_frame(self, frame):
        # Process each video frame for object detection and overlays
        detections = self.object_detector.detect_objects(frame)
        self.update_overlay(frame, detections)
    def update_overlay(self, frame, detections):
        # Update the video overlay with detected objects
        for detection in detections:
            x, y, w, h = detection['bbox']
            cv2.rectangle(frame, (x, y), (x + w, y + h), (0, 255, 0), 2)
        cv2.imshow('Sports App', frame)
        cv2.waitKey(1)
if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = SportsApp()

object_detector.py
```python
'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''
import cv2
import numpy as np
class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)
    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections
    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                score = detection[4]
                if score > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    bbox = detection[:4].astype(int)
                    detections.append({'bbox': bbox, 'score': score})
        return detections
```

video_processor.py
```python
'''
Video processing class that captures video frames from the camera.
'''
import cv2
class VideoProcessor:
    def __init__(self):
        self.capture = cv2.VideoCapture(0)
    def get_frame(self):
        # Capture a frame from the video feed
        ret, frame = self.capture.read()
        if not ret:
            return None
        return frame
    def __del__(self):
        self.capture.release()
```

**main.py**
```python
'''
Main application file for the sports app that handles video processing and overlays.
'''
from app_gui import AppGUI
from video_processor import VideoProcessor
from object_detector import ObjectDetector
import cv2

class SportsApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.video_processor = VideoProcessor()
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
        self.gui = AppGUI(self.start_video)

    def load_model(self):
        # Load the YOLO model using ONNX
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')

    def start_video(self):
        # Start capturing video from the camera
        self.load_model()  # Ensure the model is loaded before starting video
        while True:
            frame = self.video_processor.get_frame()
            if frame is None:
                break
            self.process_frame(frame)

    def process_frame(self, frame):
        # Process each video frame for object detection and overlays
        detections = self.object_detector.detect_objects(frame)
        self.update_overlay(frame, detections)

    def update_overlay(self, frame, detections):
        # Update the video overlay with detected objects
        for detection in detections:
            x, y, w, h = detection['bbox']
            cv2.rectangle(frame, (x, y), (x + w, y + h), (0, 255, 0), 2)
        cv2.imshow('Sports App', frame)
        cv2.waitKey(1)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = SportsApp()
```

**object_detector.py**
```python
'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''
import cv2
import numpy as np

class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)

    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections

    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                score = detection[4]
                if score > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    bbox = detection[:4].astype(int)
                    detections.append({'bbox': bbox, 'score': score})
        return detections
```

```python
'''
Main application file for the sports app that handles video processing and overlays.
'''
from app_gui import AppGUI
from video_processor import VideoProcessor
from object_detector import ObjectDetector
import cv2

class SportsApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.video_processor = VideoProcessor()
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
        self.gui = AppGUI(self.start_video)

    def load_model(self):
        # Load the YOLO model using ONNX
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')

    def start_video(self):
        # Start capturing video from the camera
        self.load_model()  # Ensure the model is loaded before starting video
        while True:
            frame = self.video_processor.get_frame()
            if frame is None:
                break
            self.process_frame(frame)

    def process_frame(self, frame):
        # Process each video frame for object detection and overlays
        detections = self.object_detector.detect_objects(frame)
        self.update_overlay(frame, detections)

    def update_overlay(self, frame, detections):
        # Update the video overlay with detected objects
        for detection in detections:
            x, y, w, h = detection['bbox']
            cv2.rectangle(frame, (x, y), (x + w, y + h), (0, 255, 0), 2)
        cv2.imshow('Sports App', frame)
        cv2.waitKey(1)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = SportsApp()

**object_detector.py**
```python
'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''
import cv2
import numpy as np

class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)

    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections

    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                score = detection[4]
                if score > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    bbox = detection[:4].astype(int)
                    detections.append({'bbox': bbox, 'score': score})
        return detections
```

from app_gui import AppGUI
from video_processor import VideoProcessor
from object_detector import ObjectDetector
import cv2
class SportsApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.video_processor = VideoProcessor()
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
        self.gui = AppGUI(self.start_video)
    def load_model(self):
        # Load the YOLO model using ONNX
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
    def start_video(self):
        # Start capturing video from the camera
        self.load_model()  # Ensure the model is loaded before starting video
        while True:
            frame = self.video_processor.get_frame()
            if frame is None:
                break
            self.process_frame(frame)
    def process_frame(self, frame):
        # Process each video frame for object detection and overlays
        detections = self.object_detector.detect_objects(frame)
        self.update_overlay(frame, detections)
    def update_overlay(self, frame, detections):
        # Update the video overlay with detected objects
        for detection in detections:
            x, y, w, h = detection['bbox']
            cv2.rectangle(frame, (x, y), (x + w, y + h), (0, 255, 0), 2)
        cv2.imshow('Sports App', frame)
        cv2.waitKey(1)
if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = SportsApp()
```

object_detector.py
```python
'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''
import cv2
import numpy as np
class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)
    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections
    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                score = detection[4]
                if score > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    bbox = detection[:4].astype(int)
                    detections.append({'bbox': bbox, 'score': score})
        return detections
```

video_processor.py
```python
'''
Video processing class that captures video frames from the camera.
'''
import cv2
class VideoProcessor:
    def __init__(self):
        self.capture = cv2.VideoCapture(0)
    def get_frame(self):
        # Capture a frame from the video feed
        ret, frame = self.capture.read()
        if not ret:
            return None
        return frame
    def __del__(self):
        self.capture.release()
```

### Suggestions for Revision:

2. **Add Error Handling**: Implement error handling in the `detect_objects` method to manage cases where the model fails to produce valid outputs.

Here is a revised version of the `process_outputs` method:

```python
def process_outputs(self, outputs):
    # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
    detections = []
    for output in outputs:
        for detection in output:
            scores = detection[5:]  # Assuming the first 5 values are x, y, w, h, and confidence
            class_id = np.argmax(scores)
            confidence = scores[class_id]
            if confidence > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                center_x, center_y, width, height = detection[:4]
                x = int((center_x - width / 2))
                y = int((center_y - height / 2))
                detections.append({'bbox': [x, y, int(width), int(height)], 'score': confidence, 'class_id': class_id})
    return detections
```

"main.py
```python
'''
Main application file for the sports app that handles video processing and overlays.
'''
from app_gui import AppGUI
from video_processor import VideoProcessor
from object_detector import ObjectDetector
import cv2
class SportsApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.video_processor = VideoProcessor()
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
        self.gui = AppGUI(self.start_video)
    def load_model(self):
        # Load the YOLO model using ONNX
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
    def start_video(self):
        # Start capturing video from the camera
        self.load_model()  # Ensure the model is loaded before starting video
        while True:
            frame = self.video_processor.get_frame()
            if frame is None:
                break
            self.process_frame(frame)
    def process_frame(self, frame):
        # Process each video frame for object detection and overlays
        detections = self.object_detector.detect_objects(frame)
        self.update_overlay(frame, detections)
    def update_overlay(self, frame, detections):
        # Update the video overlay with detected objects
        for detection in detections:
            x, y, w, h = detection['bbox']
            cv2.rectangle(frame, (x, y), (x + w, y + h), (0, 255, 0), 2)
        cv2.imshow('Sports App', frame)
        cv2.waitKey(1)
if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = SportsApp()
```

object_detector.py
```python
'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''
import cv2
import numpy as np
class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)
    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections
    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                score = detection[4]
                if score > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    bbox = detection[:4].astype(int)
                    detections.append({'bbox': bbox, 'score': score})
        return detections
```

video_processor.py
```python
'''
Video processing class that captures video frames from the camera.
'''
import cv2
class VideoProcessor:
    def __init__(self):
        self.capture = cv2.VideoCapture(0)
    def get_frame(self):
        # Capture a frame from the video feed
        ret, frame = self.capture.read()
        if not ret:
            return None
        return frame
    def __del__(self):
        self.capture.release()
```

**main.py**
```python
'''
Main application file for the sports app that handles video processing and overlays.
'''
from app_gui import AppGUI
from video_processor import VideoProcessor
from object_detector import ObjectDetector
import cv2

class SportsApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.video_processor = VideoProcessor()
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
        self.gui = AppGUI(self.start_video)

    def load_model(self):
        # Load the YOLO model using ONNX
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')

    def start_video(self):
        # Start capturing video from the camera
        self.load_model()  # Ensure the model is loaded before starting video
        while True:
            frame = self.video_processor.get_frame()
            if frame is None:
                break
            self.process_frame(frame)

    def process_frame(self, frame):
        # Process each video frame for object detection and overlays
        detections = self.object_detector.detect_objects(frame)
        self.update_overlay(frame, detections)

    def update_overlay(self, frame, detections):
        # Update the video overlay with detected objects
        for detection in detections:
            x, y, w, h = detection['bbox']
            cv2.rectangle(frame, (x, y), (x + w, y + h), (0, 255, 0), 2)
        cv2.imshow('Sports App', frame)
        cv2.waitKey(1)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = SportsApp()
```

**object_detector.py**
```python
'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''
import cv2
import numpy as np

class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)

    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections

    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                scores = detection[5:]  # Assuming the first 5 values are x, y, w, h, and confidence
                class_id = np.argmax(scores)
                confidence = scores[class_id]
                if confidence > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    center_x, center_y, width, height = detection[:4]
                    x = int((center_x - width / 2))
                    y = int((center_y - height / 2))
                    detections.append({'bbox': [x, y, int(width), int(height)], 'score': confidence, 'class_id': class_id})
        return detections
```

**video_processor.py**
```python
'''
Video processing class that captures video frames from the camera.
'''
import cv2

class VideoProcessor:
    def __init__(self):
        self.capture = cv2.VideoCapture(0)

    def get_frame(self):
        # Capture a frame from the video feed
        ret, frame = self.capture.read()
        if not ret:
            return None
        return frame

    def __del__(self):
        self.capture.release()
```

'''
Graphical user interface class for the sports app using Tkinter.
'''
import tkinter as tk

class AppGUI:
    def __init__(self, start_video_callback):
        self.window = tk.Tk()
        self.window.title("Sports App")
        self.start_button = tk.Button(self.window, text="Start Video", command=start_video_callback)
        self.start_button.pack()
        self.window.mainloop()
```

from app_gui import AppGUI
from video_processor import VideoProcessor
from object_detector import ObjectDetector
import cv2

class SportsApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.video_processor = VideoProcessor()
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
        self.gui = AppGUI(self.start_video)

        # Load the YOLO model using ONNX
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')

    def start_video(self):

        while True:
            frame = self.video_processor.get_frame()
            if frame is None:
                break
            self.process_frame(frame)

    def process_frame(self, frame):
        # Process each video frame for object detection and overlays
        detections = self.object_detector.detect_objects(frame)
        self.update_overlay(frame, detections)

    def update_overlay(self, frame, detections):
        # Update the video overlay with detected objects
        for detection in detections:

        cv2.imshow('Sports App', frame)

if __name__ == "__main__":

**object_detector.py**
```python
'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''
import cv2
import numpy as np

class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)

    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections

    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                scores = detection[5:]  # Assuming the first 5 values are x, y, w, h, and confidence
                class_id = np.argmax(scores)
                confidence = scores[class_id]
                if confidence > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    center_x, center_y, width, height = detection[:4]
                    x = int((center_x - width / 2))
                    y = int((center_y - height / 2))
                    detections.append({'bbox': [x, y, int(width), int(height)], 'score': confidence, 'class_id': class_id})
        return detections
```

"main.py
```python
'''
Main application file for the sports app that handles video processing and overlays.
'''
from app_gui import AppGUI
from video_processor import VideoProcessor
from object_detector import ObjectDetector
import cv2
class SportsApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.video_processor = VideoProcessor()
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
        self.gui = AppGUI(self.start_video)
    def load_model(self):
        # Load the YOLO model using ONNX
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
    def start_video(self):
        # Start capturing video from the camera
        self.load_model()  # Ensure the model is loaded before starting video
        while True:
            frame = self.video_processor.get_frame()
            if frame is None:
                break
            self.process_frame(frame)
    def process_frame(self, frame):
        # Process each video frame for object detection and overlays
        detections = self.object_detector.detect_objects(frame)
        self.update_overlay(frame, detections)
    def update_overlay(self, frame, detections):
        # Update the video overlay with detected objects
        for detection in detections:
            x, y, w, h = detection['bbox']
            cv2.rectangle(frame, (x, y), (x + w, y + h), (0, 255, 0), 2)
        cv2.imshow('Sports App', frame)
        cv2.waitKey(1)
if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = SportsApp()
```

object_detector.py
```python
'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''
import cv2
import numpy as np
class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)
    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections
    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                scores = detection[5:]  # Assuming the first 5 values are x, y, w, h, and confidence
                class_id = np.argmax(scores)
                confidence = scores[class_id]
                if confidence > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    center_x, center_y, width, height = detection[:4]
                    x = int((center_x - width / 2))
                    y = int((center_y - height / 2))
                    detections.append({'bbox': [x, y, int(width), int(height)], 'score': confidence, 'class_id': class_id})
        return detections
```

video_processor.py
```python
'''
Video processing class that captures video frames from the camera.
'''
import cv2
class VideoProcessor:
    def __init__(self):
        self.capture = cv2.VideoCapture(0)
    def get_frame(self):
        # Capture a frame from the video feed
        ret, frame = self.capture.read()
        if not ret:
            return None
        return frame
    def __del__(self):
        self.capture.release()
```

import tkinter as tk

class AppGUI:
    def __init__(self, start_video_callback, stop_video_callback):
        self.window = tk.Tk()
        self.window.title("Sports App")
        self.start_button = tk.Button(self.window, text="Start Video", command=start_video_callback)
        self.start_button.pack()

        self.video_processor = VideoProcessor()

        self.running = True  # Set the running flag

"main.py
```python
'''
Main application file for the sports app that handles video processing and overlays.
'''
from app_gui import AppGUI
from video_processor import VideoProcessor
from object_detector import ObjectDetector
import cv2
class SportsApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.video_processor = VideoProcessor()
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
        self.gui = AppGUI(self.start_video)
    def load_model(self):
        # Load the YOLO model using ONNX
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
    def start_video(self):
        # Start capturing video from the camera
        self.load_model()  # Ensure the model is loaded before starting video
        while True:
            frame = self.video_processor.get_frame()
            if frame is None:
                break
            self.process_frame(frame)
    def process_frame(self, frame):
        # Process each video frame for object detection and overlays
        detections = self.object_detector.detect_objects(frame)
        self.update_overlay(frame, detections)
    def update_overlay(self, frame, detections):
        # Update the video overlay with detected objects
        for detection in detections:
            x, y, w, h = detection['bbox']
            cv2.rectangle(frame, (x, y), (x + w, y + h), (0, 255, 0), 2)
        cv2.imshow('Sports App', frame)
        cv2.waitKey(1)
if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = SportsApp()

object_detector.py
```python
'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''
import cv2
import numpy as np
class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)
    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections
    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                scores = detection[5:]  # Assuming the first 5 values are x, y, w, h, and confidence
                class_id = np.argmax(scores)
                confidence = scores[class_id]
                if confidence > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    center_x, center_y, width, height = detection[:4]
                    x = int((center_x - width / 2))
                    y = int((center_y - height / 2))
                    detections.append({'bbox': [x, y, int(width), int(height)], 'score': confidence, 'class_id': class_id})
        return detections
```

video_processor.py
```python
'''
Video processing class that captures video frames from the camera.
'''
import cv2
class VideoProcessor:
    def __init__(self):
        self.capture = cv2.VideoCapture(0)
    def get_frame(self):
        # Capture a frame from the video feed
        ret, frame = self.capture.read()
        if not ret:
            return None
        return frame
    def __del__(self):
        self.capture.release()
```

**main.py**
```python
'''
Main application file for the sports app that handles video processing and overlays.
'''
from app_gui import AppGUI
from video_processor import VideoProcessor
from object_detector import ObjectDetector
import cv2

class SportsApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.video_processor = VideoProcessor()
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
        self.gui = AppGUI(self.start_video)

    def load_model(self):
        # Load the YOLO model using ONNX
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')

    def start_video(self):
        # Start capturing video from the camera
        self.load_model()  # Ensure the model is loaded before starting video
        while True:
            frame = self.video_processor.get_frame()
            if frame is None:
                break
            self.process_frame(frame)

    def process_frame(self, frame):
        # Process each video frame for object detection and overlays
        detections = self.object_detector.detect_objects(frame)
        self.update_overlay(frame, detections)

    def update_overlay(self, frame, detections):
        # Update the video overlay with detected objects
        for detection in detections:
            x, y, w, h = detection['bbox']
            cv2.rectangle(frame, (x, y), (x + w, y + h), (0, 255, 0), 2)
        cv2.imshow('Sports App', frame)
        cv2.waitKey(1)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = SportsApp()
```

'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''
import cv2
import numpy as np

class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)

    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections

    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                scores = detection[5:]  # Assuming the first 5 values are x, y, w, h, and confidence
                class_id = np.argmax(scores)
                confidence = scores[class_id]
                if confidence > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    center_x, center_y, width, height = detection[:4]
                    x = int((center_x - width / 2))
                    y = int((center_y - height / 2))
                    detections.append({'bbox': [x, y, int(width), int(height)], 'score': confidence, 'class_id': class_id})
        return detections
```

'''

'''
from app_gui import AppGUI
from video_processor import VideoProcessor
from object_detector import ObjectDetector
import cv2

class SportsApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.video_processor = VideoProcessor()
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
        self.gui = AppGUI(self.start_video)

    def load_model(self):
        # Load the YOLO model using ONNX
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')

    def start_video(self):
        # Start capturing video from the camera
        self.load_model()  # Ensure the model is loaded before starting video
        while True:
            frame = self.video_processor.get_frame()
            if frame is None:
                break
            self.process_frame(frame)

    def process_frame(self, frame):

        detections = self.object_detector.detect_objects(frame)
        self.update_overlay(frame, detections)

        for detection in detections:

```python
'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''
import cv2
import numpy as np

class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)

    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections

    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                scores = detection[5:]  # Assuming the first 5 values are x, y, w, h, and confidence
                class_id = np.argmax(scores)
                confidence = scores[class_id]
                if confidence > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    center_x, center_y, width, height = detection[:4]
                    x = int((center_x - width / 2))
                    y = int((center_y - height / 2))
                    detections.append({'bbox': [x, y, int(width), int(height)], 'score': confidence, 'class_id': class_id})
        return detections
```

Task: "Please help me implement a Python program to optimize object tracking and real-time video overlays for a sports app utilizing YOLO, ONNX, and a hybrid LLM, ensuring compatibility for mobile device use.".

"main.py
```python
'''
Main application file for the sports app that handles video processing and overlays.
'''
from app_gui import AppGUI
from video_processor import VideoProcessor
from object_detector import ObjectDetector
import cv2
class SportsApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.video_processor = VideoProcessor()
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
        self.gui = AppGUI(self.start_video)
    def load_model(self):
        # Load the YOLO model using ONNX
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
    def start_video(self):
        # Start capturing video from the camera
        self.load_model()  # Ensure the model is loaded before starting video
        while True:
            frame = self.video_processor.get_frame()
            if frame is None:
                break
            self.process_frame(frame)
    def process_frame(self, frame):
        # Process each video frame for object detection and overlays
        detections = self.object_detector.detect_objects(frame)
        self.update_overlay(frame, detections)
    def update_overlay(self, frame, detections):
        # Update the video overlay with detected objects
        for detection in detections:
            x, y, w, h = detection['bbox']
            cv2.rectangle(frame, (x, y), (x + w, y + h), (0, 255, 0), 2)
        cv2.imshow('Sports App', frame)
        cv2.waitKey(1)
if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = SportsApp()
```

object_detector.py
```python
'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''
import cv2
import numpy as np
class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)
    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections
    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                scores = detection[5:]  # Assuming the first 5 values are x, y, w, h, and confidence
                class_id = np.argmax(scores)
                confidence = scores[class_id]
                if confidence > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    center_x, center_y, width, height = detection[:4]
                    x = int((center_x - width / 2))
                    y = int((center_y - height / 2))
                    detections.append({'bbox': [x, y, int(width), int(height)], 'score': confidence, 'class_id': class_id})
        return detections
```

video_processor.py
```python
'''
Video processing class that captures video frames from the camera.
'''
import cv2
class VideoProcessor:
    def __init__(self):
        self.capture = cv2.VideoCapture(0)
    def get_frame(self):
        # Capture a frame from the video feed
        ret, frame = self.capture.read()
        if not ret:
            return None
        return frame
    def __del__(self):
        self.capture.release()
```

class AppGUI:

        self.window = tk.Tk()
        self.window.title("Sports App")
        self.start_button = tk.Button(self.window, text="Start Video", command=start_video_callback)
        self.start_button.pack()
        self.window.mainloop()

Task: "Please help me implement a Python program to optimize object tracking and real-time video overlays for a sports app utilizing YOLO, ONNX, and a hybrid LLM, ensuring compatibility for mobile device use.".

"main.py
```python
'''
Main application file for the sports app that handles video processing and overlays.
'''
from app_gui import AppGUI
from video_processor import VideoProcessor
from object_detector import ObjectDetector
import cv2
class SportsApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.video_processor = VideoProcessor()
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
        self.gui = AppGUI(self.start_video)
    def load_model(self):
        # Load the YOLO model using ONNX
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
    def start_video(self):
        # Start capturing video from the camera
        self.load_model()  # Ensure the model is loaded before starting video
        while True:
            frame = self.video_processor.get_frame()
            if frame is None:
                break
            self.process_frame(frame)
    def process_frame(self, frame):
        # Process each video frame for object detection and overlays
        detections = self.object_detector.detect_objects(frame)
        self.update_overlay(frame, detections)
    def update_overlay(self, frame, detections):
        # Update the video overlay with detected objects
        for detection in detections:
            x, y, w, h = detection['bbox']
            cv2.rectangle(frame, (x, y), (x + w, y + h), (0, 255, 0), 2)
        cv2.imshow('Sports App', frame)
        cv2.waitKey(1)
if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = SportsApp()
```

object_detector.py
```python
'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''
import cv2
import numpy as np
class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)
    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections
    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                scores = detection[5:]  # Assuming the first 5 values are x, y, w, h, and confidence
                class_id = np.argmax(scores)
                confidence = scores[class_id]
                if confidence > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    center_x, center_y, width, height = detection[:4]
                    x = int((center_x - width / 2))
                    y = int((center_y - height / 2))
                    detections.append({'bbox': [x, y, int(width), int(height)], 'score': confidence, 'class_id': class_id})
        return detections
```

    def __init__(self):

    def get_frame(self):
        # Capture a frame from the video feed

**main.py**
```python
'''
Main application file for the sports app that handles video processing and overlays.
'''
from app_gui import AppGUI
from video_processor import VideoProcessor
from object_detector import ObjectDetector
import cv2

class SportsApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.video_processor = VideoProcessor()
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
        self.gui = AppGUI(self.start_video)

    def load_model(self):
        # Load the YOLO model using ONNX
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')

    def start_video(self):
        # Start capturing video from the camera
        self.load_model()  # Ensure the model is loaded before starting video
        while True:
            frame = self.video_processor.get_frame()
            if frame is None:
                break
            self.process_frame(frame)

    def process_frame(self, frame):
        # Process each video frame for object detection and overlays
        detections = self.object_detector.detect_objects(frame)
        self.update_overlay(frame, detections)

    def update_overlay(self, frame, detections):
        # Update the video overlay with detected objects
        for detection in detections:
            x, y, w, h = detection['bbox']
            cv2.rectangle(frame, (x, y), (x + w, y + h), (0, 255, 0), 2)
        cv2.imshow('Sports App', frame)
        cv2.waitKey(1)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = SportsApp()
```

```python
'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''
import cv2
import numpy as np

class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)

    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections

    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                scores = detection[5:]  # Assuming the first 5 values are x, y, w, h, and confidence
                class_id = np.argmax(scores)
                confidence = scores[class_id]
                if confidence > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    center_x, center_y, width, height = detection[:4]
                    x = int((center_x - width / 2))
                    y = int((center_y - height / 2))
                    detections.append({'bbox': [x, y, int(width), int(height)], 'score': confidence, 'class_id': class_id})
        return detections
```

**main.py**
```python
'''
Main application file for the sports app that handles video processing and overlays.
'''
from app_gui import AppGUI
from video_processor import VideoProcessor
from object_detector import ObjectDetector
import cv2

class SportsApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.video_processor = VideoProcessor()
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
        self.gui = AppGUI(self.start_video)

    def load_model(self):
        # Load the YOLO model using ONNX
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')

    def start_video(self):
        # Start capturing video from the camera
        self.load_model()  # Ensure the model is loaded before starting video
        while True:
            frame = self.video_processor.get_frame()
            if frame is None:
                break
            self.process_frame(frame)

    def process_frame(self, frame):
        # Process each video frame for object detection and overlays
        detections = self.object_detector.detect_objects(frame)
        self.update_overlay(frame, detections)

    def update_overlay(self, frame, detections):
        # Update the video overlay with detected objects
        for detection in detections:
            x, y, w, h = detection['bbox']
            cv2.rectangle(frame, (x, y), (x + w, y + h), (0, 255, 0), 2)
        cv2.imshow('Sports App', frame)
        cv2.waitKey(1)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = SportsApp()
```

**object_detector.py**
```python
'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''
import cv2
import numpy as np

class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)

    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections

    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                scores = detection[5:]  # Assuming the first 5 values are x, y, w, h, and confidence
                class_id = np.argmax(scores)
                confidence = scores[class_id]
                if confidence > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    center_x, center_y, width, height = detection[:4]
                    x = int((center_x - width / 2))
                    y = int((center_y - height / 2))
                    detections.append({'bbox': [x, y, int(width), int(height)], 'score': confidence, 'class_id': class_id})
        return detections
```

object_detector.py
```python
'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''
import cv2
import numpy as np
class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)
    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections
    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                scores = detection[5:]  # Assuming the first 5 values are x, y, w, h, and confidence
                class_id = np.argmax(scores)
                confidence = scores[class_id]
                if confidence > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    center_x, center_y, width, height = detection[:4]
                    x = int((center_x - width / 2))
                    y = int((center_y - height / 2))
                    detections.append({'bbox': [x, y, int(width), int(height)], 'score': confidence, 'class_id': class_id})
        return detections
```

video_processor.py
```python
'''
Video processing class that captures video frames from the camera.
'''
import cv2
class VideoProcessor:
    def __init__(self):
        self.capture = cv2.VideoCapture(0)
    def get_frame(self):
        # Capture a frame from the video feed
        ret, frame = self.capture.read()
        if not ret:
            return None
        return frame
    def __del__(self):
        self.capture.release()
```

```plaintext
'''
Main application file for the sports app that handles video processing and overlays.
'''
from app_gui import AppGUI
from video_processor import VideoProcessor
from object_detector import ObjectDetector
import cv2
class SportsApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.video_processor = VideoProcessor()
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
        self.gui = AppGUI(self.start_video)
    def load_model(self):
        # Load the YOLO model using ONNX
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
    def start_video(self):
        # Start capturing video from the camera
        self.load_model()  # Ensure the model is loaded before starting video
        while True:
            frame = self.video_processor.get_frame()
            if frame is None:
                break
            self.process_frame(frame)
    def process_frame(self, frame):
        # Process each video frame for object detection and overlays
        detections = self.object_detector.detect_objects(frame)
        self.update_overlay(frame, detections)
    def update_overlay(self, frame, detections):
        # Update the video overlay with detected objects
        for detection in detections:
            x, y, w, h = detection['bbox']
            cv2.rectangle(frame, (x, y), (x + w, y + h), (0, 255, 0), 2)
        cv2.imshow('Sports App', frame)
        cv2.waitKey(1)
if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = SportsApp()
```

```plaintext
'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''
import cv2
import numpy as np
class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)
    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections
    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                scores = detection[5:]  # Assuming the first 5 values are x, y, w, h, and confidence
                class_id = np.argmax(scores)
                confidence = scores[class_id]
                if confidence > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    center_x, center_y, width, height = detection[:4]
                    x = int((center_x - width / 2))
                    y = int((center_y - height / 2))
                    detections.append({'bbox': [x, y, int(width), int(height)], 'score': confidence, 'class_id': class_id})
        return detections
```

        while True:

                break
            self.process_frame(frame)

'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''
import cv2
import numpy as np
class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)
    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections
    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                scores = detection[5:]  # Assuming the first 5 values are x, y, w, h, and confidence
                class_id = np.argmax(scores)
                confidence = scores[class_id]
                if confidence > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    center_x, center_y, width, height = detection[:4]
                    x = int((center_x - width / 2))
                    y = int((center_y - height / 2))
                    detections.append({'bbox': [x, y, int(width), int(height)], 'score': confidence, 'class_id': class_id})
        return detections
```

```python
'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''
import cv2
import numpy as np
class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)
    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections
    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                scores = detection[5:]  # Assuming the first 5 values are x, y, w, h, and confidence
                class_id = np.argmax(scores)
                confidence = scores[class_id]
                if confidence > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    center_x, center_y, width, height = detection[:4]
                    x = int((center_x - width / 2))
                    y = int((center_y - height / 2))
                    detections.append({'bbox': [x, y, int(width), int(height)], 'score': confidence, 'class_id': class_id})
        return detections
```

video_processor.py
```python
'''
Video processing class that captures video frames from the camera.
'''
import cv2
class VideoProcessor:
    def __init__(self):
        self.capture = cv2.VideoCapture(0)
    def get_frame(self):
        # Capture a frame from the video feed
        ret, frame = self.capture.read()
        if not ret:
            return None
        return frame
    def __del__(self):
        self.capture.release()
```

```python
'''
Main application file for the sports app that handles video processing and overlays.
'''
from app_gui import AppGUI
from video_processor import VideoProcessor
from object_detector import ObjectDetector
import cv2
class SportsApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.video_processor = VideoProcessor()
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
        self.gui = AppGUI(self.start_video)
    def load_model(self):
        # Load the YOLO model using ONNX
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
    def start_video(self):
        # Start capturing video from the camera
        self.load_model()  # Ensure the model is loaded before starting video
        while True:
            frame = self.video_processor.get_frame()
            if frame is None:
                break
            self.process_frame(frame)
    def process_frame(self, frame):
        # Process each video frame for object detection and overlays
        detections = self.object_detector.detect_objects(frame)
        self.update_overlay(frame, detections)
    def update_overlay(self, frame, detections):
        # Update the video overlay with detected objects
        for detection in detections:
            x, y, w, h = detection['bbox']
            cv2.rectangle(frame, (x, y), (x + w, y + h), (0, 255, 0), 2)
        cv2.imshow('Sports App', frame)
        cv2.waitKey(1)
if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = SportsApp()
```

FILENAME
```python
'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''
import cv2
import numpy as np
class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)
    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections
    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                scores = detection[5:]  # Assuming the first 5 values are x, y, w, h, and confidence
                class_id = np.argmax(scores)
                confidence = scores[class_id]
                if confidence > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    center_x, center_y, width, height = detection[:4]
                    x = int((center_x - width / 2))
                    y = int((center_y - height / 2))
                    detections.append({'bbox': [x, y, int(width), int(height)], 'score': confidence, 'class_id': class_id})
        return detections
```

```python
'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''
import cv2
import numpy as np
class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)
    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections
    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                scores = detection[5:]  # Assuming the first 5 values are x, y, w, h, and confidence
                class_id = np.argmax(scores)
                confidence = scores[class_id]
                if confidence > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    center_x, center_y, width, height = detection[:4]
                    x = int((center_x - width / 2))
                    y = int((center_y - height / 2))
                    detections.append({'bbox': [x, y, int(width), int(height)], 'score': confidence, 'class_id': class_id})
        return detections
```

'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''
import cv2
import numpy as np
class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)
    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections
    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                scores = detection[5:]  # Assuming the first 5 values are x, y, w, h, and confidence
                class_id = np.argmax(scores)
                confidence = scores[class_id]
                if confidence > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    center_x, center_y, width, height = detection[:4]
                    x = int((center_x - width / 2))
                    y = int((center_y - height / 2))
                    detections.append({'bbox': [x, y, int(width), int(height)], 'score': confidence, 'class_id': class_id})
        return detections
```

video_processor.py
```python
'''
Video processing class that captures video frames from the camera.
'''
import cv2
class VideoProcessor:
    def __init__(self):
        self.capture = cv2.VideoCapture(0)
    def get_frame(self):
        # Capture a frame from the video feed
        ret, frame = self.capture.read()
        if not ret:
            return None
        return frame
    def __del__(self):
        self.capture.release()
```

The new user's task and our developed codes are listed: 

Task: "Please help me implement a Python program to optimize object tracking and real-time video overlays for a sports app utilizing YOLO, ONNX, and a hybrid LLM, ensuring compatibility for mobile device use.".

Programming Language: " Python *"

"main.py
```python
'''
Main application file for the sports app that handles video processing and overlays.
'''
from app_gui import AppGUI
from video_processor import VideoProcessor
from object_detector import ObjectDetector
import cv2
class SportsApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.video_processor = VideoProcessor()
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
        self.gui = AppGUI(self.start_video)
    def load_model(self):
        # Load the YOLO model using ONNX
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
    def start_video(self):
        # Start capturing video from the camera
        self.load_model()  # Ensure the model is loaded before starting video
        while True:
            frame = self.video_processor.get_frame()
            if frame is None:
                break
            self.process_frame(frame)
    def process_frame(self, frame):
        # Process each video frame for object detection and overlays
        detections = self.object_detector.detect_objects(frame)
        self.update_overlay(frame, detections)
    def update_overlay(self, frame, detections):
        # Update the video overlay with detected objects
        for detection in detections:
            x, y, w, h = detection['bbox']
            cv2.rectangle(frame, (x, y), (x + w, y + h), (0, 255, 0), 2)
        cv2.imshow('Sports App', frame)
        cv2.waitKey(1)
if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = SportsApp()
```

object_detector.py
```python
'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''
import cv2
import numpy as np
class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)
    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections
    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                scores = detection[5:]  # Assuming the first 5 values are x, y, w, h, and confidence
                class_id = np.argmax(scores)
                confidence = scores[class_id]
                if confidence > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    center_x, center_y, width, height = detection[:4]
                    x = int((center_x - width / 2))
                    y = int((center_y - height / 2))
                    detections.append({'bbox': [x, y, int(width), int(height)], 'score': confidence, 'class_id': class_id})
        return detections
```

Task: "Please help me implement a Python program to optimize object tracking and real-time video overlays for a sports app utilizing YOLO, ONNX, and a hybrid LLM, ensuring compatibility for mobile device use.".

"main.py
```python
'''
Main application file for the sports app that handles video processing and overlays.
'''
from app_gui import AppGUI
from video_processor import VideoProcessor
from object_detector import ObjectDetector
import cv2
class SportsApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.video_processor = VideoProcessor()
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
        self.gui = AppGUI(self.start_video)
    def load_model(self):
        # Load the YOLO model using ONNX
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
    def start_video(self):
        # Start capturing video from the camera
        self.load_model()  # Ensure the model is loaded before starting video
        while True:
            frame = self.video_processor.get_frame()
            if frame is None:
                break
            self.process_frame(frame)
    def process_frame(self, frame):
        # Process each video frame for object detection and overlays
        detections = self.object_detector.detect_objects(frame)
        self.update_overlay(frame, detections)
    def update_overlay(self, frame, detections):
        # Update the video overlay with detected objects
        for detection in detections:
            x, y, w, h = detection['bbox']
            cv2.rectangle(frame, (x, y), (x + w, y + h), (0, 255, 0), 2)
        cv2.imshow('Sports App', frame)
        cv2.waitKey(1)
if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = SportsApp()
```
object_detector.py
```python
'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''
import cv2
import numpy as np
class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)
    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections
    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                scores = detection[5:]  # Assuming the first 5 values are x, y, w, h, and confidence
                class_id = np.argmax(scores)
                confidence = scores[class_id]
                if confidence > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    center_x, center_y, width, height = detection[:4]
                    x = int((center_x - width / 2))
                    y = int((center_y - height / 2))
                    detections.append({'bbox': [x, y, int(width), int(height)], 'score': confidence, 'class_id': class_id})
        return detections
```
video_processor.py
```python
'''
Video processing class that captures video frames from the camera.
Note: Ensure OpenCV is installed in your environment. You can install it using:
pip install opencv-python
'''
import cv2
class VideoProcessor:
    def __init__(self):
        self.capture = cv2.VideoCapture(0)
    def get_frame(self):
        # Capture a frame from the video feed
        ret, frame = self.capture.read()
        if not ret:
            return None
        return frame
    def __del__(self):
        self.capture.release()
```
app_gui.py
```python
'''
Graphical user interface class for the sports app using Tkinter.
'''
import tkinter as tk
class AppGUI:
    def __init__(self, start_video_callback):
        self.window = tk.Tk()
        self.window.title("Sports App")
        self.start_button = tk.Button(self.window, text="Start Video", command=start_video_callback)
        self.start_button.pack()
        self.window.mainloop()
```

The new user's task, our developed codes and required dependencies are listed: 

Task: "Please help me implement a Python program to optimize object tracking and real-time video overlays for a sports app utilizing YOLO, ONNX, and a hybrid LLM, ensuring compatibility for mobile device use.".

Programming Language: " Python *"

"main.py
```python
'''
Main application file for the sports app that handles video processing and overlays.
'''
from app_gui import AppGUI
from video_processor import VideoProcessor
from object_detector import ObjectDetector
import cv2
class SportsApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.video_processor = VideoProcessor()
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
        self.gui = AppGUI(self.start_video)
    def load_model(self):
        # Load the YOLO model using ONNX
        self.object_detector = ObjectDetector('yolo_model.onnx')
    def start_video(self):
        # Start capturing video from the camera
        self.load_model()  # Ensure the model is loaded before starting video
        while True:
            frame = self.video_processor.get_frame()
            if frame is None:
                break
            self.process_frame(frame)
    def process_frame(self, frame):
        # Process each video frame for object detection and overlays
        detections = self.object_detector.detect_objects(frame)
        self.update_overlay(frame, detections)
    def update_overlay(self, frame, detections):
        # Update the video overlay with detected objects
        for detection in detections:
            x, y, w, h = detection['bbox']
            cv2.rectangle(frame, (x, y), (x + w, y + h), (0, 255, 0), 2)
        cv2.imshow('Sports App', frame)
        cv2.waitKey(1)
if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = SportsApp()
```

object_detector.py
```python
'''
Object detection class that uses YOLO model for detecting objects in video frames.
'''
import cv2
import numpy as np
class ObjectDetector:
    def __init__(self, model_path):
        self.net = cv2.dnn.readNetFromONNX(model_path)
    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Run the detection on a given frame
        blob = cv2.dnn.blobFromImage(frame, 1/255.0, (640, 640), swapRB=True, crop=False)
        self.net.setInput(blob)
        outputs = self.net.forward()
        detections = self.process_outputs(outputs)
        return detections
    def process_outputs(self, outputs):
        # Process the outputs to extract bounding boxes and class IDs
        detections = []
        for output in outputs:
            for detection in output:
                scores = detection[5:]  # Assuming the first 5 values are x, y, w, h, and confidence
                class_id = np.argmax(scores)
                confidence = scores[class_id]
                if confidence > 0.5:  # Confidence threshold
                    center_x, center_y, width, height = detection[:4]
                    x = int((center_x - width / 2))
                    y = int((center_y - height / 2))
                    detections.append({'bbox': [x, y, int(width), int(height)], 'score': confidence, 'class_id': class_id})
        return detections
```

video_processor.py
```python
'''
Video processing class that captures video frames from the camera.
Note: Ensure OpenCV is installed in your environment. You can install it using:
pip install opencv-python
'''
import cv2
class VideoProcessor:
    def __init__(self):
        self.capture = cv2.VideoCapture(0)
    def get_frame(self):
        # Capture a frame from the video feed
        ret, frame = self.capture.read()
        if not ret:
            return None
        return frame
    def __del__(self):
        self.capture.release()
```

app_gui.py
```python
'''
Graphical user interface class for the sports app using Tkinter.
'''
import tkinter as tk
class AppGUI:
    def __init__(self, start_video_callback):
        self.window = tk.Tk()
        self.window.title("Sports App")
        self.start_button = tk.Button(self.window, text="Start Video", command=start_video_callback)
        self.start_button.pack()
        self.window.mainloop()

# LangChain

Building applications with LLMs through composability

Looking for the JS/TS version? Check out LangChain.js.

**Production Support:** As you move your LangChains into production, we'd love to offer more comprehensive support.

Please fill out this form and we'll set up a dedicated support Slack channel.

## Quick Install

`pip install langchain`

or

`conda install langchain -c conda-forge`

## 🤔 What is this?

Large language models (LLMs) are emerging as a transformative technology, enabling developers to build applications that they previously could not. However, using these LLMs in isolation is often insufficient for creating a truly powerful app - the real power comes when you can combine them with other sources of computation or knowledge.

This library aims to assist in the development of those types of applications. Common examples of these applications include:

**❓ Question Answering over specific documents**

- Documentation

- End-to-end Example: Question Answering over Notion Database

**🤖 Agents**

- Documentation

- End-to-end Example: GPT+WolframAlpha

## 📖 Documentation

Please see [here](https://python.langchain.com) for full documentation on:

- Getting started (installation, setting up the environment, simple examples)

- How-To examples (demos, integrations, helper functions)

- Reference (full API docs)

- Resources (high-level explanation of core concepts)

# Sports App User Manual

## Introduction

The Sports App is designed to provide real-time video processing and object tracking for sports applications. Utilizing advanced technologies such as YOLO (You Only Look Once) for object detection, ONNX (Open Neural Network Exchange) for model optimization, and a hybrid LLM (Large Language Model) for enhanced functionality, this application aims to deliver an engaging experience for sports enthusiasts.

### Main Functions

- **Real-Time Video Processing**: Captures video from the camera and processes each frame for object detection.
- **Object Detection**: Utilizes the YOLO model to identify and track objects within the video feed.
- **Video Overlays**: Displays bounding boxes around detected objects in real-time.
- **User Interface**: A simple GUI built with Tkinter to start video processing.

## Installation

To set up the environment and install the necessary dependencies, follow these steps:

1. **Clone the Repository**: If you haven't already, clone the repository containing the application code.

   ```bash
   git clone <repository-url>
   cd <repository-directory>
   ```

2. **Create a Virtual Environment** (optional but recommended):

   ```bash
   python -m venv venv
   source venv/bin/activate  # On Windows use `venv\Scripts\activate`
   ```

3. **Install Dependencies**: Use the `requirements.txt` file to install the required packages.

   ```bash
   pip install -r requirements.txt
   ```

   The `requirements.txt` includes:
   - **opencv-python**: For video processing and object detection.
   - **numpy**: For numerical operations.
   - **onnxruntime**: For running the ONNX model.

## How to Use

1. **Run the Application**: Start the application by executing the `main.py` file.

   ```bash
   python main.py
   ```

2. **Start Video Processing**: Once the application is running, a GUI window will appear with a "Start Video" button. Click this button to begin capturing video from your camera.

3. **View Object Detection**: As the video is processed, the application will display bounding boxes around detected objects in real-time.

4. **Stop the Application**: To stop the video processing, simply close the application window.

## Additional Notes

- Ensure that your camera is connected and accessible by the application.
- The application is optimized for mobile device compatibility; however, performance may vary based on the device's hardware capabilities.
- Adjust the confidence threshold in the `object_detector.py` file if necessary to fine-tune detection accuracy.

## Support

For any issues or questions, please reach out to our support team via the contact information provided in the repository.

Thank you for using the Sports App! Enjoy tracking your favorite sports in real-time!
```
